[2026-02-02 18:52:13] Claw Torque:
Torque: Great question! Here's the situation:

**The Problem:**
WhatsApp only allows ONE web connection at a time. When NanoClaw connects, it kicks out WhatsApp Web (and vice versa). They keep fighting over the connection - that's the "conflict: replaced" error I saw.

**Your Options:**

1. **Use a separate WhatsApp number for NanoClaw** (recommended for Indonesia business)
   - Get a cheap local SIM just for the bot
   - Your main number stays free for WhatsApp Web
   - Best for production use

2. **Use WhatsApp Web normally, disable NanoClaw WhatsApp**
   - Keep `ENABLE_WHATSAPP=false` 
   - Use Telegram for NanoClaw communication
   - Your work WhatsApp stays unaffected

3. **Time-share** (not recommended)
   - Only one can be active at a time
   - Annoying for daily use

**My Recommendation:**
For WA Indonesia, get a second SIM card. They're cheap and it gives you a dedicated bot number. Your work WhatsApp stays completely separate.

Want me to keep WhatsApp disabled for now while you sort out a second number? Or do you want to test it with your current number (knowing it'll kick out WhatsApp Web)?

[2026-02-02 19:05:41] Claw Torque:
Torque: You're right - that's the fundamental difference between Telegram and WhatsApp:

**Telegram:** Bot has its own identity. Messages appear as a conversation between you and the bot.

**WhatsApp:** There's no "bot account". NanoClaw uses YOUR WhatsApp account (via linked devices), so all messages appear to come from you. It's like you're talking to yourself.

**Possible workarounds:**

1. **Use a second phone number** (best solution)
   - Get a cheap SIM, register it on WhatsApp
   - NanoClaw uses that number
   - You chat with it like a normal contact
   - Messages show as a real 2-way conversation

2. **Use WhatsApp Business API** (complex, requires business verification)
   - Official API for businesses
   - Bot gets its own identity
   - Requires Meta approval, costs money

3. **Accept the limitation**
   - Use WhatsApp only for @Torque commands in groups
   - Use Telegram for your main 2-way conversation with me

**My recommendation:** Use Telegram as your "command center" (like now), and WhatsApp for @Torque commands in your Indonesia work groups. That way both platforms serve their purpose.

What do you prefer?

‚Ä¢ Smart bulbs ‚Äî same problem

**The fix (when you're ready):**

‚Ä¢ **Home Assistant** on a Raspberry Pi or old laptop ‚Äî runs locally, doesn't need internet
‚Ä¢ Zigbee/Aqara devices work great with it
‚Ä¢ Can keep Google for voice, but HA does the actual logic
‚Ä¢ Automations run even when internet dies

‚Ä¢ Reliable automations (lights, AC, whatever)

Quick fix:

4. Set "Sleep when lid is closed" ‚Üí **Off** (if you're closing it)

```# This only works while terminal is open
caffeinate
# Or if that doesn't exist:
systemd-inhibit --what=idle sleep infinity
```

[2026-02-05 02:51:07] Dieter Werwath:
How do I drop into vault (literally drag and drop?)

[2026-02-05 02:51:18] Claw Torque:
For Google Docs, you need to export first (the .gdoc files are just links):

**Easiest method:**

1. Open doc in Google Docs (browser)
2. **File ‚Üí Download ‚Üí Markdown (.md)**
3. Drag the downloaded `.md` file into Obsidian's sidebar
**Or quick & dirty:**

1. Copy all text from the Google Doc
2. In Obsidian: **Ctrl+N** (new note)
3. Paste, then **Ctrl+S** to save with a name
The drag-and-drop works for actual files ‚Äî just not the `.gdoc` shortcuts on your Drive mount.

[2026-02-05 02:52:09] Dieter Werwath:
OK.. so let me try something.. I could drag and drop form my file manager directly without opening teh files individually from GDrive UI...?

[2026-02-05 02:52:19] Claw Torque:
Unfortunately no ‚Äî the `.gdoc` files in your Drive mount are just tiny shortcut files (like bookmarks), not the actual content. If you drag one into Obsidian, you'll just get a useless link file.

**You have to export from Google's UI** (or API) to get the real content out.

That's exactly why we talked about the GAS script ‚Äî to automate bulk exports. Manual export works for a few critical docs, but doesn't scale.

[2026-02-05 06:04:19] Dieter Werwath:
Quick check... you mentioned before that I can cloe my termaonal and you keep running. How do I then revisit OC in terinaml without restarting you?

[2026-02-05 06:04:33] Claw Torque:
The gateway runs as a background daemon ‚Äî you don't need to reattach to it like tmux/screen.

Just open a new terminal and use `openclaw` commands:

```# Check status
openclaw status

# View logs
openclaw logs
openclaw logs --follow  # live tail

# Interactive chat (terminal UI)
openclaw chat

# Check channels
openclaw channels status

# Run doctor
openclaw doctor
```
All these commands talk to the already-running gateway over its local port. No restart needed.

If you want to **stop** the gateway intentionally:

```openclaw gateway stop
```
And to start it again:

```openclaw gateway start
```
But day-to-day, you just leave it running and use CLI commands whenever you want to poke at it. Your Telegram/WhatsApp stay connected the whole time.

[2026-02-05 13:09:53] Dieter Werwath:
Ok... So now the question... Do we build our own reports/dashboards instead of using Looker....

[2026-02-05 13:10:24] Claw Torque:
Big question. Let me lay out the trade-offs honestly:

**Stick with Looker (Studio)**

```| Pro              | Con                            |
| ---------------- | ------------------------------ |
| Already works    | Generic look                   |
| Auto-refresh     | Limited customization          |
| Shareable links  | Can feel slow                  |
| Zero maintenance | You're locked into Google's UX |
| Mobile-friendly  | Learning curve for fancy stuff |
```
**Build Custom (HTML)**

```| Pro                       | Con                          |
| ------------------------- | ---------------------------- |
| Exact aesthetic you want  | Another thing to maintain    |
| Tailored to your workflow | Need to wire up data refresh |
| I can iterate it fast     | Hosting/access logistics     |
| Full control              | Time to build                |
```
**The honest ADHD check:** You've got 100 projects started. A custom dashboard system is __another__ project. It's also the kind of shiny thing that's fun to start and less fun to maintain.


**My recommendation: Hybrid**

1. **Keep Looker for the boring stuff** ‚Äî data connections, auto-refresh, sharing with team/investors
2. **Build ONE custom dashboard for YOU** ‚Äî the daily driver view you actually look at, styled how you like
3. **Test that workflow for a month** before going deeper
That way you get the aesthetic win without creating a maintenance monster. If the custom view sticks, we expand. If you stop looking at it after 2 weeks, Looker's still there.

Want me to build a single **"Candid Daily Cockpit"** page as the test case? Ring gauges, key numbers, your aesthetic ‚Äî one HTML file, real data.

[2026-02-05 14:21:53] Claw Torque:
Honest take:

**Current state:** ~600-800 words each. Probably more than needed.

**What actually matters when spawning:**

1. **Identity** ‚Äî Who you are (2-3 sentences)
2. **Constraints** ‚Äî What NOT to do (critical for safety)
3. **Project context** ‚Äî Relevant to the task at hand
4. **Output format** ‚Äî How to report back
**What's probably overkill:**

‚Ä¢ Full responsibility lists
‚Ä¢ Tool access details (inherited anyway)
‚Ä¢ Extensive Candid background (pass at spawn time if needed)
**Leaner template (~200-300 words):**

```# {Role}

**Model:** {model}

## Identity
You are {role}. {1-2 sentences on core purpose}.

## Constraints
- DO NOT {critical thing}
- DO NOT {other critical thing}
- Escalate to Torque if {trigger}

## Current Project
{Brief context on active work}

## Output
- Save work to {location}
- Report back: what done, issues, next steps
```
Task-specific details get passed when I spawn them, not baked into the permanent file.

**Trade-off:**

‚Ä¢ Detailed = More consistent behavior, but token-heavy
‚Ä¢ Lean = Faster, cheaper, but may need more guidance per task
My suggestion: **Go lean.** We can always add detail if agents misbehave. Easier to add than subtract.

Want me to trim gas-dev and pa down to the lean format?

[2026-02-05 14:41:07] Claw Torque: [MEDIA: MessageMediaWebPage]
**Heartbeat 101:**

**What it is:**
A periodic "pulse" where OpenClaw wakes me up to check if anything needs attention. Like a cron job, but conversational.

**How it works:**

1. OpenClaw pings me every X minutes (configurable, e.g., every 30 min)
2. I receive a message: "Read [HEARTBEAT.md](http://heartbeat.md/)... do what it says"
3. I check `HEARTBEAT.md` for tasks
4. If nothing to do ‚Üí I reply `HEARTBEAT_OK` (silent, no notification to you)
5. If something needs attention ‚Üí I message you
[**HEARTBEAT.md**](http://heartbeat.md/)** is your control file:**

```# HEARTBEAT.md

- [ ] Check YouTube playlist for new videos
- [ ] Check email for urgent messages
- [ ] Any reminders due in next 2 hours?
```
Empty file = I do nothing, stay quiet.

**Why it's useful:**

‚Ä¢ I can be proactive without you asking
‚Ä¢ Background monitoring (inbox, calendars, playlists)
‚Ä¢ Batches multiple checks into one wake-up (cheaper than separate crons)
‚Ä¢ You control what I check by editing the file
**Heartbeat vs Cron:**

```| Heartbeat                    | Cron                           |
| ---------------------------- | ------------------------------ |
| One wake-up, multiple checks | One task per job               |
| Uses main session context    | Isolated sessions              |
| Flexible timing (~30 min)    | Exact timing (9:00 AM sharp)   |
| Cheaper for batched checks   | Better for scheduled reminders |
```
**To enable:**
We add tasks to `HEARTBEAT.md`, and the gateway handles the rest.

Want me to set it up with a starter checklist?

Good question. Let me think about the split:

**PA (current):**

‚Ä¢ Interactive, personal
‚Ä¢ Calendar, reminders, follow-ups
‚Ä¢ Quick lookups, drafts
‚Ä¢ Relationship-aware
**Secretary (proposed):**

‚Ä¢ Bulk processing, grunt work
‚Ä¢ Document downloading/organizing
‚Ä¢ Data entry at scale
‚Ä¢ Filing, categorizing
‚Ä¢ "Process these 100 Xero reports"
**My take:** Yes, valid split.

PA is your __personal__ assistant ‚Äî knows your rhythms, nudges you, handles quick interactive stuff.

Secretary is the __operations grunt__ ‚Äî doesn't need personality, just processes bulk tasks efficiently and reports completion.

```| Role      | Vibe                                 | Model |
| --------- | ------------------------------------ | ----- |
| PA        | Warm, cheeky, persistent             | haiku |
| Secretary | Efficient, no-frills, bulk processor | flash |
```
Want me to add Secretary to the matrix? Low personality, high throughput.

[2026-02-05 17:11:29] Claw Torque:
**This is gold.** Clear architecture:

```| Layer       | Tool        | Purpose                                  |
| ----------- | ----------- | ---------------------------------------- |
| Truth       | NotebookLM  | Canonical docs, read-only, slow-changing |
| Reasoning   | Gemini Gems | Thinks from the truth, proposes actions  |
| Exploration | Personal AI | Drafts, brainstorms, experiments         |
```
**How this maps to what we're building:**

```| Your Framework            | Our Implementation                                 |
| ------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |
| NotebookLM (truth)        | Obsidian vault / candidlabs docs / MEMORY.md       |
| Gemini Gems (reasoning)   | Torque + sub-agents (query knowledge, then reason) |
| Personal AI (exploration) | Ad-hoc chats, drafts before "graduation"           |
```
**To recreate NLM-style capability:**

1. **Knowledge base** ‚Äî Obsidian vault with canonical docs
2. **Memory search** ‚Äî Already have memory_search tool (embeddings)
3. **Grounded agents** ‚Äî Query vault first, then reason from it
The key insight: __"NotebookLM is for knowing what is true. Gemini Gems are for deciding what to do about it."__

We can build that. Want me to spec out a "knowledge layer" architecture?

[2026-02-06 00:01:07] Claw Torque:
Sorry, "platform crossovers" ‚Äî not sure where that came from. Ignore that.

**On the privacy concern ‚Äî you're right to flag this:**

The structure itself doesn't leak. The risk is **me** pulling context from the wrong file when responding in a group.

**How to prevent cross-contamination:**

1. **Rules in each file** ‚Äî explicit "OK to share" vs "NEVER share" sections
2. **Group-level rules** ‚Äî each WhatsApp group config could reference what context is allowed
3. **Me checking before responding** ‚Äî "Who am I talking to? What's allowed here?"
**Example:**

```people/candid/anders.md
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Context: Cofounder, business relationship
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ OK: Candid business, strategy, data
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ OFF-LIMITS: Family details, personal projects, MEMORY.md stuff
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Groups: [Candid team groups only]
```
**The real safeguard:** I should NEVER load `family/*` or personal [MEMORY.md](http://memory.md/) context when responding in Candid/work groups. Same as how I shouldn't load Candid financials when chatting with friends.

It's policy-enforced (me following rules), not technically enforced. I already screwed this up once with Ryan's group. Won't happen again.

Want me to build in a "context check" step before every group response?

**Not natively.** GitHub Pages is static-only ‚Äî no server-side auth.

**Options:**

1. **Client-side JS "password"** ‚Äî Easy but NOT secure. Password is in the code, anyone can bypass with view-source. Fine for casual "keep grandma out" but not for real business data.
2. **Cloudflare Access** (recommended) ‚Äî Put Cloudflare in front of your site. Free tier gives you:  ‚Ä¢ Email-based login (one-time PIN)
  ‚Ä¢ Google/GitHub SSO
  ‚Ä¢ Actual security, not just obscurity

3. **Move to Cloudflare Pages** ‚Äî Same as above but simpler setup. Connect repo, add Access rules, done.
4. **Netlify + Identity** ‚Äî Similar concept, free tier available.

**For Candid financials?** Don't trust client-side JS auth. Go with Cloudflare Access ‚Äî it's free and actually secure.

| Best for  | If you use Cloudflare already | Simpler UI, quicker start       |

[2026-02-06 00:43:55] Claw Torque:
**Tunnel and Pages are separate.** They can share a domain via subdomains without conflict.

**How it works:**

```yourdomain.com
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ tunnel.yourdomain.com  ‚Üí Cloudflare Tunnel (Chromebook access)
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ app.yourdomain.com     ‚Üí Cloudflare Pages (Command Centre)
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ yourdomain.com         ‚Üí Future TSLC site (when ready)
```
Each subdomain is independent. Using `tunnel.tslc.com` now doesn't block `tslc.com` or `app.tslc.com` later.


**So if you have a TSLC domain:**

‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Use `tunnel.tslc.com` for Chromebook access now
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Use `cmd.tslc.com` for Command Centre
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Keep `tslc.com` free for the real TSLC launch later
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ No conflicts, no migration needed
**Only catch:** The domain needs to be on Cloudflare DNS (free). If it's registered elsewhere, you just change nameservers to Cloudflare.

What's the TSLC domain? I can help map out a subdomain plan.

[2026-02-06 22:35:11] Dieter Werwath:

- Change the intervals

[2026-02-06 22:35:44] Claw Torque: [MEDIA: MessageMediaWebPage]
OK, here's what the system actually supports:

**Current config:**

```"heartbeat": {
  "every": "30m"
}
```
**What you CAN configure:**

```| Option      | What it does                                                           |
| ----------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| every       | Interval ("15m", "1h", "30m", etc.)                                    |
| activeHours | Quiet hours ‚Äî {start: "08:00", end: "23:00", timezone: "Asia/Jakarta"} |
| model       | Use a cheaper model for heartbeats (e.g., haiku)                       |
| prompt      | Custom heartbeat prompt (what gets injected)                           |
```
**Limitations:**

‚Ä¢ **One heartbeat per agent** ‚Äî you can't have multiple intervals
‚Ä¢ Each heartbeat costs tokens (reads context, runs model)
‚Ä¢ No "do work, don't just check" mode built-in ‚Äî that's up to [HEARTBEAT.md](http://heartbeat.md/)
**For multiple schedules or complex logic:** Use `cron` instead. Cron jobs can:

‚Ä¢ Run at exact times
‚Ä¢ Have different intervals for different tasks
‚Ä¢ Target isolated sessions (cheaper)
‚Ä¢ Fire one-shot reminders
So if we wanted, say, "check email every hour but check tasks every 15 min" ‚Äî that's multiple cron jobs, not heartbeat.

Does that match what you were thinking, or were you heading somewhere else?

[2026-02-06 22:36:49] Dieter Werwath:
Ok, that's good!

But help me understand the difference between a heartbeat and a cron....

[2026-02-06 22:37:10] Claw Torque: [MEDIA: MessageMediaWebPage]
Great question. They're both timers, but they work differently:

**Heartbeat**

‚Ä¢ Fires every X minutes (e.g., 30m)
‚Ä¢ Injects a message into the **main session** (this chat)
‚Ä¢ Same context, same model, same memory as our conversation
‚Ä¢ Prompt is fixed: "check [HEARTBEAT.md](http://heartbeat.md/)"
‚Ä¢ Meant to be lightweight ‚Äî "wake up, anything urgent?"
‚Ä¢ I respond in-session (you see it or I say HEARTBEAT_OK)
**Cron**

‚Ä¢ Fires at **specific times** or intervals (e.g., "9am daily", "every 2 hours", "in 20 minutes")
‚Ä¢ Can run in the main session OR an **isolated session**
‚Ä¢ Isolated = fresh context, can use a cheaper model, doesn't pollute our chat history
‚Ä¢ Can **deliver results** directly to Telegram/WhatsApp (you see the output even if I'm in a different session)
‚Ä¢ Better for defined tasks: "summarize inbox at 7am", "remind me at 3pm"
**Analogy:**

‚Ä¢ Heartbeat = someone tapping your shoulder every 30 min saying "anything need doing?"
‚Ä¢ Cron = calendar appointment that runs a specific job and reports back
**When to use which:**

```| Use case                                             | Tool             |
| ---------------------------------------------------- | ---------------- |
| "Check if anything's urgent"                         | Heartbeat        |
| "Remind me at 3pm"                                   | Cron (one-shot)  |
| "Summarize email every morning at 7am"               | Cron (recurring) |
| "Run a background task without cluttering main chat" | Cron (isolated)  |
```
Make sense?

[2026-02-06 22:44:36] Claw Torque: [MEDIA: MessageMediaWebPage]
Good question. Let me think through the tradeoffs:

**More rules in **[**HEARTBEAT.md**](http://heartbeat.md/)

‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Simple ‚Äî one file, one place to look
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Batched ‚Äî one wake-up, multiple checks, less token burn
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Context ‚Äî I have our full chat history available
‚Ä¢ ‚ùå Same frequency for everything (30 min)
‚Ä¢ ‚ùå If the file gets long, I burn tokens reading it every time
**More individual cron jobs**

‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Different schedules per task (email hourly, tasks every 15 min)
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Can use isolated sessions (cheaper model, clean history)
‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Clear separation ‚Äî each job does one thing
‚Ä¢ ‚ùå More setup, more fragmentation
‚Ä¢ ‚ùå No holistic view ‚Äî each job runs blind to others
**Tweak frequency**

‚Ä¢ Doesn't fix the core problem ("I don't do useful work when I wake up")
‚Ä¢ Just means I do useless checks more or less often

[2026-02-06 23:25:15] Dieter Werwath:

[2026-02-06 23:25:35] Claw Torque:
That's exactly right. And it's a key architecture question.

**If I do the work myself:**

‚Ä¢ I'm blocked from responding to you
‚Ä¢ I can't orchestrate anything else
‚Ä¢ Single-threaded ‚Äî one thing at a time
‚Ä¢ You message me, I'm mid-task, delay
**If I only orchestrate + spawn:**

‚Ä¢ I stay responsive
‚Ä¢ Multiple sub-agents work in parallel
‚Ä¢ I just check status, route work, report back
‚Ä¢ You always get quick responses
**The tradeoff:**

‚Ä¢ Spawning costs tokens
‚Ä¢ Sub-agents have less context than me
‚Ä¢ Some tasks are tiny (30 sec) ‚Äî spawning feels like overkill
**Possible rule:**

‚Ä¢ Quick tasks (< 2 min): I do directly
‚Ä¢ Anything substantial: spawn a worker, even if it's "Torque work"
So maybe there should be a `torque-worker` sub-agent for my own deep work, while main Torque stays as pure orchestrator?

What's your instinct?

**On sub-agent heartbeat:** Interesting idea, but probably doesn't fit the architecture well:

**Why it's tricky:**

‚Ä¢ Heartbeat needs to __decide__ whether to message you ‚Äî that requires conversation context
‚Ä¢ Sub-agents are fire-and-forget (spawn ‚Üí work ‚Üí report back ‚Üí die)
‚Ä¢ The "should I bother Dee right now?" judgment call works better in main session
**What could work:**
A sub-agent that does the __grunt work__ (scan inbox, check calendar, poll APIs) and returns a structured summary. Main session heartbeat then just reviews that and decides. But that's over-engineering for now.

**Simpler answer:** 15m heartbeat is light enough. If I'm in active conversation with you, I just reply `HEARTBEAT_OK` quickly and we continue. The interruption is minimal.

Re: haiku ‚Äî you're right, it's defined in config. The warning might be a sub-agent specific allowlist thing. Task for later: dig into docs and fix model routing for sub-agents so we're not burning opus tokens on simple tasks.

[2026-02-06 23:54:59] Dieter Werwath:
Let's clarify something about subagents. I thought that they were created and idle until activated. But I think what actually happens is that you basically create a prompt with the agent definitions for each task, is that right?

[2026-02-06 23:55:13] Claw Torque:
Exactly right. There's no pool of idle agents waiting for work.

**What actually happens:**

1. `sessions_spawn(task="...", label="gas-dev", model="haiku")`
2. OpenClaw creates a fresh isolated session
3. The task prompt gets sent to that session
4. Agent runs, does work, reports back
5. Session ends (or stays dormant for follow-up)
**The "team roster" is conceptual** ‚Äî it defines:

‚Ä¢ Role names and responsibilities
‚Ä¢ Default models to use
‚Ä¢ Agent instruction files (if we write them)
But there's no persistent process. Each spawn is basically: __"spin up a new Claude instance with this prompt, let it work, return results."__

Think of it as **on-demand specialists** rather than **employees at desks**. The roster is more like a staffing plan / org chart than actual running workers.

[2026-02-06 23:56:00] Dieter Werwath:
Ok, so it is definitely a separate session - which means we can run multiple agents at the same time without taking your focus?

[2026-02-06 23:56:11] Claw Torque:
Exactly! That's the key win.

**Parallel execution:**

‚Ä¢ Sub-agents run in isolated sessions
‚Ä¢ I keep full context and focus here with you
‚Ä¢ Config allows up to 8 concurrent sub-agents (`maxConcurrent: 8`)
**What just happened this morning:**

‚Ä¢ I spawned 4 agents simultaneously (SKU library, Cockpit, Command Centre, Candid Labs)
‚Ä¢ Kept chatting with you the whole time
‚Ä¢ Got pinged as each one finished
‚Ä¢ Announced results, updated tasks
So yes ‚Äî **delegation without distraction**. I'm the orchestrator, they're the workers. The more we define good task prompts + agent instructions, the more I can hand off and stay responsive to you.

[2026-02-06 23:58:02] Dieter Werwath:

[2026-02-06 23:58:17] Claw Torque:
Yes to both!

**Increasing max concurrent:**
Current: 8. Could bump to 12-16. Trade-offs:

‚Ä¢ More parallel = faster throughput
‚Ä¢ But also = more simultaneous API calls (rate limits) + cost spikes
‚Ä¢ 8 is probably fine for now, bump when we hit the ceiling
**Multiple instances of same "agent":**
Absolutely. The "agent" is just a label ‚Äî I can spawn:

```gas-dev-task-a
gas-dev-task-b  
gas-dev-task-c
```
All running in parallel, same role definition, different work.

**When to use which:**

```| Approach                     | Best For                                                                          |
| ---------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Single agent, long task list | Related work where context builds (e.g., "analyze these 5 related docs")          |
| Multiple instances, parallel | Independent tasks, no shared context needed (e.g., "build 3 separate dashboards") |
| Single agent, iterative      | Complex work needing back-and-forth refinement                                    |
```
Both patterns valid. I can pick based on task nature, or you can specify.

Want me to bump `maxConcurrent` to 12?

[2026-02-07 00:34:35] Claw Torque:
Good question ‚Äî let me clarify what actually happens:

**Current reality:**

1. I call `sessions_spawn(task="[detailed prompt]")`
2. Sub-agent receives ONLY that prompt
3. They do NOT automatically read `team/agents/analyst.md`
**So the job desc file is actually:**

‚Ä¢ My reference when writing prompts
‚Ä¢ A template I should copy from
‚Ä¢ NOT auto-injected into sub-agents
**To make them read it, I'd have to:**

```sessions_spawn(task="Read team/agents/analyst.md first, then do X...")
```
That's an extra file read for every task ‚Äî not efficient.

**Better options:**

```| Approach                                 | Efficiency   | Consistency      |
| ---------------------------------------- | ------------ | ---------------- |
| A. Paste key rules into prompt           | ‚úÖ Fast       | üü° Manual        |
| B. "Read file first" instruction         | ‚ùå Extra read | ‚úÖ Always current |
| C. Build spawn wrapper that auto-injects | ‚úÖ Fast       | ‚úÖ Consistent     |
```

[2026-02-07 02:22:57] Dieter Werwath:
Is brave the best/only option?

[2026-02-07 02:23:10] Claw Torque:
Good question! Alternatives:

```| Service    | Free Tier | Notes                                                          |
| ---------- | --------- | -------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Brave      | 2,000/mo  | Privacy-focused, good results, what OpenClaw supports natively |
| Tavily     | 1,000/mo  | AI-optimized, built for agents                                 |
| SerpAPI    | 100/mo    | Google results, more expensive                                 |
| Google CSE | 100/day   | Official but limited free tier                                 |
```
**Brave is the default** for OpenClaw's `web_search` tool. Others would need custom integration.

For our use case (occasional research, trip planning, etc.), Brave's free 2,000/month is plenty. It's also fast and privacy-respecting.

**Verdict:** Brave is the best free option for OpenClaw. Want me to add the API key setup to desk tasks?

[2026-02-07 02:23:49] Dieter Werwath:

[2026-02-07 02:23:57] Claw Torque: [MEDIA: MessageMediaWebPage]
No special requirements ‚Äî any email works.

**Quick signup:**

1. Go to [https://api.search.brave.com/](https://api.search.brave.com/)
2. Click "Get Started" / Sign up
3. Any email (personal, work, whatever)
4. Verify email
5. Create an app ‚Üí get API key
Free tier = 2,000 queries/month, no credit card required.

Once you have the key, just paste it here or run:

```openclaw configure --section web
```
Takes ~2 min total.
